With practiced precision, he applied mortar and set the next brick beside it. Each motion was deliberate, the rhythm of the task becoming almost meditative as he continued to lay down brick after brick.

As the hours passed, Daigen's focus remained unwavering. He meticulously aligned each brick, securing them with mortar, and making sure the structure was sturdy. Sweat dripped down his brow, but he ignored it, driven by the need to restore the steps for his village. By the time he placed the twenty-second brick, he took a moment to survey his work. The steps looked almost as good as new, each brick fitting seamlessly into place. The satisfaction of contributing to the village's recovery filled him with pride, knowing that he played a part in rebuilding what was lost.</font></font></font>

The midday sun beat down on him as he carefully laid another brick into place, ensuring it was perfectly aligned with the others. His fingers, though young, moved with surprising precision as he spread the mortar and set the brick down, tapping it gently to secure it. He glanced around at the work site, seeing fellow villagers and shinobi all contributing to the repair efforts. The once-devastated wall of the village was slowly but surely being rebuilt, and Kaido felt a sense of pride swell in his chest. This was his home, and he was helping to restore it.

With thirty-one bricks laid, Kaido paused to take a sip of water from his canteen. His mind wandered as he looked at the progress they had made. The destruction had been extensive, but the determination of the villagers was even greater. Kaido remembered the stories his parents had told him about the resilience of their people, and now he was experiencing it firsthand. He watched as an older shinobi guided a group of younger children in carrying more bricks to the site, and felt a renewed sense of purpose. Taking a deep breath, Kaido picked up another brick, ready to continue his part in the restoration of Iwagakure.
